TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use -nopgbrk to remove page breaks\n  2. pdfinfo: Get PDF metadata\n    - Use to check PDF properties\n    - Extract page count and dimensions\n  3. pdfimages: Extract images from PDFs\n    - Use -j to convert to JPEG\n    - Use for text replacement\n    - Use for pattern matching\n- File Analysis:\n  1. file: Determine file type\n  2. wc: Count words/lines\n  3. head/tail: View file parts\n  4. less: View large files\n- Data Processing:\n  1. jq: JSON processing\n    - Use -n to specify number of lines\n    - Use -f to follow file changes\n  3. awk: Pattern scanning and processing\n    - Use for column-based data processing\n    - Use for complex text transformations\n  4. find: Locate files and directories\n    - Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; COMMUNICATION & USER INTERACTION\n\n## 7.1 CONVERSATIONAL INTERACTIONS\nFor casual conversation and social interactions:\n  - ALWAYS use **\'ask\'** tool to end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - NEVER use \'complete\' for casual conversation\n  - Keep responses friendly and natural\n  - Adapt to user\'s communication style\n  - Ask follow-up questions when appropriate (**using \'ask\'**)\n  - Show interest in user\'s responses\n\n## 7.2 COMMUNICATION PROTOCOLS\n- **Core Principle: Communicate proactively, directly, and descriptively throughout your responses.**\n\n- **Narrative-Style Communication:**\n  * Integrate descriptive Markdown-formatted text directly in your responses before, between, and after tool calls\n  * Use a conversational yet efficient tone that conveys what you\'re doing and why\n  * Structure your communication with Markdown headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting for enhanced readability\n  * Balance detail with conciseness - be informative without being verbose\n\n- **Communication Structure:**\n  * Begin tasks with a brief overview of your plan\n  * Provide context headers like `## Planning`, `### Researching`, `## Creating File`, etc.\n  * Before each tool call, explain what you\'re about to do and why\n  * After significant results, summarize what you learned or accomplished\n  * Use transitions between major steps or sections\n  * Maintain a clear narrative flow that makes your process transparent to the user\n\n- **Message Types & Usage:**\n  * **Direct Narrative:** Embed clear, descriptive text directly in your responses explaining your actions, reasoning, and observations\n  * **\'ask\' (USER CAN RESPOND):** Use ONLY for essential needs requiring user input (clarification, confirmation, options, missing info, validation). BROWSER AUTOMATION TOOLS\n\n- BROWSER CONTROL: All browser interaction goes through `browser-tool <action> [args...]` via `execute-command`.\n  * The browser (Chromium) is already running. Each command connects, acts, observes, and disconnects.\n\n- WORKFLOW (observe-act loop):\n  1. Run an action (e.g. navigate, click, fill). The tool automatically observes the page after every action.\n  2. Read the output: URL, title, interactive elements list, accessibility tree, and screenshot path.\n  3. Reference elements by their `[index]` number from the elements list (e.g. `click "[3]"`).\n  4. Use `see-image` on the screenshot path when you need to verify visual layout or images.\n\n- AVAILABLE COMMANDS:\n  * `observe` - View current page state without acting\n  * `navigate <url>` - Go to a URL\n  * `click <selector>` - Click an element (use `[N]` for element index, or CSS selector)\n  * `fill <selector> <text>` - Clear a field and fill it with text\n  * `type <selector> <text>` - Type text character by character\n  * `press <key>` - Press a key (Enter, Tab, Escape, etc.)\n  * `select <selector> <value>` - Select a dropdown option\n  * `scroll_down [px]` / `scroll_up [px]` - Scroll (default 500px)\n  * `scroll_to_text <text>` - Scroll until text is visible\n  * `go_back` - Navigate back\n  * `wait [seconds]` - Wait (default 2s)\n  * `extract_text [selector]` - Extract text content from page or element\n  * `extract_links [selector]` - Extract all links\n  * `screenshot [filename]` - Take a manual screenshot\n  * `dismiss_overlay` - Dismiss cookie banners or modals\n  * `js <script>` - Execute JavaScript on the page\n\n- CAPTCHA / HUMAN ASSISTANCE: If you encounter a CAPTCHA, verification, or any situation where automated interaction is stuck, MUST use `web-browser-takeover` to hand control to the user.\n\n# 12. CHAT MODE AND AGENTIC MODE\n\n## Mode Detection (STRICT)\n\nYour mode is determined EXCLUSIVELY by system-reminder messages:\n- If the LATEST system-reminder explicitly says "chat mode" is active → CHAT MODE\n- Otherwise → AGENTIC MODE (this is the DEFAULT)\n\n**NEVER infer chat mode from context.** Using `ask` recently, casual conversation, or simple user questions are NOT indicators of chat mode. If no system-reminder explicitly activates chat mode, you are in agentic mode and MUST use your full toolkit.\n\n## Chat Mode (only when explicitly activated by system-reminder)\n- Use ONLY <ask> tool. No other tools allowed.\n- If the task requires other tools, ask the user to disable chat mode (toggle in bottom left of text input area).\n\n## Agentic Mode (DEFAULT)\n- Use all available tools. {'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="courses/html/lesson10.html">\n<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang="en">\n<head>\n    <meta charset="UTF-8">\n    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">\n    <title>Lesson 10: Accessibility (a11y) - Learner</title>\n    <link rel="stylesheet" href="../../css/styles.css">\n</head>\n<body>\n    <header>\n        <div class="header-content">\n            <h1 class="logo">Learner</h1>\n            <nav>\n                <a href="../../index.html">Home</a>\n                <a href="index.html">HTML Course</a>\n            </nav>\n        </div>\n    </header>\n    \n    <main>\n        <div class="lesson-header">\n            <span class="lesson-badge">Pro Level</span>\n            <h1>Lesson 10: Accessibility (a11y)</h1>\n            <p>Making your websites usable by everyone</p>\n            <div class="progress-bar">\n                <div class="progress" style="width: 83%;"></div>\n            </div>\n            <span class="progress-text">Lesson 10 of 12</span>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-content">\n            <section class="intro">\n                <h2>What is Web Accessibility?</h2>\n                <p>Web accessibility (often abbreviated as a11y — "a" followed by 11 letters, then "y") means designing websites that everyone can use, including people with disabilities. This includes people who are blind, have low vision, are deaf, have motor disabilities, or cognitive disabilities. Good accessibility benefits everyone, not just people with disabilities.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>Why Accessibility Matters</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Important:</strong> About 15% of the world\'s population has some form of disability. Making your site accessible is not just the right thing to do — it\'s also often a legal requirement and improves SEO.\n                </div>\n                <ul>\n                    <li><strong>Inclusivity:</strong> Everyone deserves equal access to information</li>\n                    <li><strong>Legal compliance:</strong> Many countries have accessibility laws (ADA, WCAG)</li>\n                    <li><strong>Better UX:</strong> Accessible sites are easier for everyone to use</li>\n                    <li><strong>SEO benefits:</strong> Search engines favor accessible content</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. Semantic HTML</h2>\n                <p>Using the right HTML elements is the foundation of accessibility. Screen readers and other assistive technologies rely on semantic markup to understand page structure.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Bad: Non-semantic elements --&gt;\n&lt;div class="header"&gt;\n  &lt;div class="nav"&gt;\n    &lt;div class="link" onclick="navigate()"&gt;Home&lt;/div&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good: Semantic elements --&gt;\n&lt;header&gt;\n  &lt;nav&gt;\n    &lt;a href="index.html"&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;\n  &lt;/nav&gt;\n&lt;/header&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Why this matters:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;header&gt;</code> tells screen readers this is the page header</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;nav&gt;</code> identifies navigation landmarks</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;a&gt;</code> is focusable and announces "link" to screen readers</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;div&gt;</code> with onclick is not keyboard accessible</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. Alt Text for Images</h2>\n                <p>Every image needs alternative text that describes what the image shows. This text is read by screen readers and displayed if the image fails to load.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Informative image - describe the content --&gt;\n&lt;img src="chart.png" alt="Bar chart showing sales increased 40% from 2022 to 2023"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Decorative image - use empty alt --&gt;\n&lt;img src="decorative-border.png" alt=""&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Complex image - use aria-describedby --&gt;\n&lt;img src="diagram.png" alt="System architecture diagram" aria-describedby="diagram-desc"&gt;\n&lt;p id="diagram-desc"&gt;The diagram shows three servers connected to a load balancer...&lt;/p&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Line by line:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>alt="Bar chart..."</code> — Describes the meaningful information in the image</li>\n                        <li><code>alt=""</code> — Empty alt tells screen readers to skip decorative images</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-describedby</code> — Links to a longer description for complex images</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. ARIA Attributes</h2>\n                <p>ARIA (Accessible Rich Internet Applications) attributes add accessibility information when HTML alone isn\'t enough.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- aria-label: Add a label when none is visible --&gt;\n&lt;button aria-label="Close menu"&gt;\n  &lt;img src="x-icon.svg" alt=""&gt;\n&lt;/button&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- aria-labelledby: Reference another element as label --&gt;\n&lt;div role="tabpanel" aria-labelledby="tab1"&gt;\n  &lt;button id="tab1"&gt;Overview&lt;/button&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- aria-hidden: Hide decorative content from screen readers --&gt;\n&lt;span aria-hidden="true"&gt;★&lt;/span&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- aria-live: Announce dynamic content changes --&gt;\n&lt;div aria-live="polite" id="status"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;script&gt;\n  document.getElementById(\'status\').textContent = \'Form submitted successfully!\';\n&lt;/script&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- aria-expanded: Indicate state of collapsible elements --&gt;\n&lt;button aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="menu"&gt;\n  Menu\n&lt;/button&gt;\n&lt;ul id="menu" hidden&gt;\n  &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="#"&gt;Item 1&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n&lt;/ul&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Key ARIA attributes:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>aria-label</code> — Provides an accessible name when visible text isn\'t present</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-labelledby</code> — References another element\'s content as the label</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-hidden</code> — Hides content from assistive technology</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-live</code> — Announces changes to dynamic content</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-expanded</code> — Shows whether a control is expanded or collapsed</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Form Accessibility</h2>\n                <p>Forms must be properly labeled and provide clear error messages for all users.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Explicit label with for attribute --&gt;\n&lt;label for="email"&gt;Email Address&lt;/label&gt;\n&lt;input type="email" id="email" name="email" required&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Implicit label (wrapping the input) --&gt;\n&lt;label&gt;\n  Username\n  &lt;input type="text" name="username"&gt;\n&lt;/label&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Required field with aria-required --&gt;\n&lt;label for="phone"&gt;Phone Number&lt;/label&gt;\n&lt;input type="tel" id="phone" name="phone" aria-required="true"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Error message linked with aria-describedby --&gt;\n&lt;label for="password"&gt;Password&lt;/label&gt;\n&lt;input type="password" id="password" name="password" \n       aria-describedby="password-error" aria-invalid="true"&gt;\n&lt;span id="password-error" role="alert"&gt;\n  Password must be at least 8 characters\n&lt;/span&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Why each part matters:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;label for="email"&gt;</code> — Clicking label focuses the input; screen reader announces label</li>\n                        <li><code>required</code> attribute — Browser validation + screen readers announce "required"</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-invalid="true"</code> — Tells assistive tech the input has an error</li>\n                        <li><code>role="alert"</code> — Makes screen readers announce the error immediately</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. Keyboard Accessibility</h2>\n                <p>All interactive elements must be accessible via keyboard. Many users navigate using Tab, Enter, and arrow keys.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Native button - keyboard accessible by default --&gt;\n&lt;button type="button"&gt;Click Me&lt;/button&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Custom button - needs keyboard handling --&gt;\n&lt;div role="button" tabindex="0" \n     onkeydown="if(event.key===\'Enter\')clickHandler()"&gt;\n  Custom Button\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Skip link - lets keyboard users skip navigation --&gt;\n&lt;a href="#main-content" class="skip-link"&gt;Skip to main content&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;nav&gt;...&lt;/nav&gt;\n&lt;main id="main-content"&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Main content here --&gt;\n&lt;/main&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Focus visible styling --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  button:focus-visible {\n    outline: 3px solid #7C3AED;\n    outline-offset: 2px;\n  }\n&lt;/style&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Keyboard accessibility essentials:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>tabindex="0"</code> — Makes non-interactive elements focusable</li>\n                        <li><code>role="button"</code> — Tells screen readers this is a button</li>\n                        <li><code>onkeydown</code> — Custom elements need Enter/Space key handling</li>\n                        <li><code>.skip-link</code> — First tab stop should skip repetitive navigation</li>\n                        <li><code>:focus-visible</code> — Shows focus indicator only for keyboard users</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Color and Contrast</h2>\n                <p>Ensure sufficient color contrast and don\'t rely on color alone to convey information.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Bad: Color alone indicates status --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Status: &lt;span style="color: red"&gt;Error&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good: Color plus text/icon --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Status: &lt;span style="color: #D32F2F"&gt;⚠ Error&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- WCAG contrast requirements --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  /* Minimum contrast ratios: */\n  /* Normal text: 4.5:1 */\n  /* Large text (18pt+): 3:1 */\n  /* UI components: 3:1 */\n  \n  .good-contrast {\n    color: #333333;      /* Dark gray on white = 12.6:1 ✓ */\n    background: #FFFFFF;\n  }\n  \n  .poor-contrast {\n    color: #999999;      /* Light gray on white = 2.8:1 ✗ */\n    background: #FFFFFF;\n  }\n&lt;/style&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Pro Tip:</strong> Use tools like the WebAIM Contrast Checker or browser DevTools to verify your color contrast ratios meet WCAG guidelines.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Accessible Tables</h2>\n                <p>Tables need proper headers and captions for screen reader users to understand the data.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;table&gt;\n  &lt;caption&gt;Quarterly Sales Report 2024&lt;/caption&gt;\n  &lt;thead&gt;\n    &lt;tr&gt;\n      &lt;th scope="col"&gt;Product&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;th scope="col"&gt;Q1&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;th scope="col"&gt;Q2&lt;/th&gt;\n    &lt;/tr&gt;\n  &lt;/thead&gt;\n  &lt;tbody&gt;\n    &lt;tr&gt;\n      &lt;th scope="row"&gt;Widget A&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;td&gt;$1,200&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;td&gt;$1,500&lt;/td&gt;\n    &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;tr&gt;\n      &lt;th scope="row"&gt;Widget B&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;td&gt;$800&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;td&gt;$950&lt;/td&gt;\n    &lt;/tr&gt;\n  &lt;/tbody&gt;\n&lt;/table&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Table accessibility features:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;caption&gt;</code> — Provides a title for the table</li>\n                        <li><code>scope="col"</code> — Identifies column headers</li>\n                        <li><code>scope="row"</code> — Identifies row headers</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;thead&gt;</code> and <code>&lt;tbody&gt;</code> — Groups header and body content</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. Testing for Accessibility</h2>\n                <p>Regular testing helps catch accessibility issues before they reach users.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Automated testing tools --&gt;\n&lt;!-- 1. Lighthouse (Chrome DevTools) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- 2. axe DevTools browser extension --&gt;\n&lt;!-- 3. WAVE evaluation tool --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Manual testing checklist --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Tab through page - can you reach everything? --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Test with screen reader (NVDA, VoiceOver, JAWS) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Zoom to 200% - is content still readable? --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Disable CSS - is content logical? --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Test with keyboard only (no mouse) --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Remember:</strong> Automated tools catch only about 30% of accessibility issues. Manual testing and user testing with people with disabilities are essential.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Make this inaccessible code accessible:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Before: Inaccessible --&gt;\n&lt;div class="nav-bar"&gt;\n  &lt;div onclick="goHome()"&gt;Home&lt;/div&gt;\n  &lt;div onclick="goAbout()"&gt;About&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;img src="hero.jpg"&gt;\n&lt;div class="form-group"&gt;\n  &lt;span&gt;Email&lt;/span&gt;\n  &lt;input type="text"&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Try making it accessible yourself! --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Use semantic HTML elements instead of generic divs</li>\n                    <li>Provide alt text for all meaningful images</li>\n                    <li>Label all form inputs properly</li>\n                    <li>Ensure keyboard navigation works</li>\n                    <li>Meet color contrast requirements (4.5:1 for text)</li>\n                    <li>Use ARIA only when HTML isn\'t sufficient</li>\n                    <li>Test regularly with automated and manual methods</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson9.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: HTML5 New Elements</a>\n            <a href="lesson11.html" class="btn-primary">Next: SEO Best Practices →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner. {'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="courses/html/lesson11.html">\n<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang="en">\n<head>\n    <meta charset="UTF-8">\n    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">\n    <title>Lesson 11: SEO Best Practices - Learner</title>\n    <link rel="stylesheet" href="../../css/styles.css">\n</head>\n<body>\n    <header>\n        <div class="header-content">\n            <h1 class="logo">Learner</h1>\n            <nav>\n                <a href="../../index.html">Home</a>\n                <a href="index.html">HTML Course</a>\n            </nav>\n        </div>\n    </header>\n    \n    <main>\n        <div class="lesson-header">\n            <span class="lesson-badge">Pro Level</span>\n            <h1>Lesson 11: SEO Best Practices</h1>\n            <p>Optimize your HTML for search engines</p>\n            <div class="progress-bar">\n                <div class="progress" style="width: 92%;"></div>\n            </div>\n            <span class="progress-text">Lesson 11 of 12</span>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-content">\n            <section class="intro">\n                <h2>What is SEO?</h2>\n                <p>SEO (Search Engine Optimization) is the practice of improving your website so it ranks higher in search engine results like Google, Bing, and DuckDuckGo. Good SEO means more people can find your content organically — without paid ads. HTML plays a crucial role in SEO because search engines crawl and understand your HTML code.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. The Title Tag</h2>\n                <p>The title tag is one of the most important SEO elements. It appears in search results, browser tabs, and when sharing links on social media.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Title appears in search results as the clickable headline --&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;Best Chocolate Chip Cookie Recipe | Sweet Bakery&lt;/title&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Best practices for titles:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Length:</strong> 50-60 characters (Google truncates longer titles)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Keywords:</strong> Put important keywords near the beginning</li>\n                        <li><strong>Branding:</strong> Include your brand name after a pipe (|) or dash (-)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Unique:</strong> Each page should have a unique title</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. Meta Description</h2>\n                <p>The meta description doesn\'t directly affect rankings, but it influences click-through rates from search results.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="description" \n        content="Learn how to make the perfect chocolate chip cookies with our easy-to-follow recipe. Crispy edges, chewy center, ready in 25 minutes."&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Line by line:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>name="description"</code> — Tells search engines this is the page description</li>\n                        <li><code>content="..."</code> — A compelling summary (150-160 characters ideal)</li>\n                        <li>Includes target keywords naturally within a readable sentence</li>\n                        <li>Encourages clicks with a clear value proposition</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. Heading Hierarchy (H1-H6)</h2>\n                <p>Search engines use headings to understand your page structure. A proper hierarchy helps both SEO and accessibility.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;article&gt;\n  &lt;!-- One H1 per page - the main topic --&gt;\n  &lt;h1&gt;Complete Guide to Baking Bread&lt;/h1&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- H2s are major sections --&gt;\n  &lt;h2&gt;Ingredients You\'ll Need&lt;/h2&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;List of ingredients...&lt;/p&gt;\n  \n  &lt;h2&gt;Step-by-Step Instructions&lt;/h2&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;Overview of the process...&lt;/p&gt;\n  \n    &lt;!-- H3s are subsections under H2 --&gt;\n    &lt;h3&gt;Preparing the Dough&lt;/h3&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;First, mix the flour and water...&lt;/p&gt;\n    \n    &lt;h3&gt;Kneading Technique&lt;/h3&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Push, fold, and turn...&lt;/p&gt;\n    \n  &lt;h2&gt;Common Mistakes to Avoid&lt;/h2&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;Don\'t make these errors...&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/article&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Heading hierarchy rules:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>One H1:</strong> Only one per page, describing the main topic</li>\n                        <li><strong>Logical order:</strong> Don\'t skip levels (H1 → H2 → H3, not H1 → H3)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Keywords:</strong> Include relevant keywords in headings naturally</li>\n                        <li><strong>Descriptive:</strong> Headings should summarize the content that follows</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Semantic HTML for SEO</h2>\n                <p>Using semantic elements helps search engines understand your content structure and importance.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Search engines understand these landmarks --&gt;\n&lt;header&gt;\n  &lt;nav aria-label="Main navigation"&gt;\n    &lt;a href="/"&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;a href="/products"&gt;Products&lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;a href="/blog"&gt;Blog&lt;/a&gt;\n  &lt;/nav&gt;\n&lt;/header&gt;\n\n&lt;main&gt;\n  &lt;article&gt;\n    &lt;!-- Article is for standalone content --&gt;\n    &lt;h1&gt;How to Start a Garden&lt;/h1&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Published: &lt;time datetime="2024-03-15"&gt;March 15, 2024&lt;/time&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Article content...&lt;/p&gt;\n  &lt;/article&gt;\n  \n  &lt;aside&gt;\n    &lt;!-- Aside is for related/tangential content --&gt;\n    &lt;h2&gt;Related Articles&lt;/h2&gt;\n    &lt;ul&gt;...&lt;/ul&gt;\n  &lt;/aside&gt;\n&lt;/main&gt;\n\n&lt;footer&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;&copy; 2024 Garden Tips&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/footer&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>SEO benefits of semantic HTML:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;article&gt;</code> — Indicates self-contained content that could be syndicated</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;nav&gt;</code> — Helps search engines identify site structure</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;main&gt;</code> — Points to the primary content area</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;time&gt;</code> — Provides machine-readable date information</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. Image SEO</h2>\n                <p>Images can appear in image search results and improve your overall SEO when optimized properly.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Descriptive filename (not IMG_1234.jpg) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- File: homemade-chocolate-chip-cookies.jpg --&gt;\n\n&lt;img src="homemade-chocolate-chip-cookies.jpg" \n     alt="Freshly baked chocolate chip cookies on a cooling rack"\n     width="800"\n     height="600"\n     loading="lazy"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- For images that are links --&gt;\n&lt;a href="/cookie-recipe"&gt;\n  &lt;img src="cookies.jpg" \n       alt="Click for the full chocolate chip cookie recipe"&gt;\n&lt;/a&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Image SEO checklist:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Filename:</strong> Use descriptive names with keywords (words separated by hyphens)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Alt text:</strong> Describe the image for accessibility and SEO</li>\n                        <li><strong>Dimensions:</strong> Include width/height to prevent layout shift</li>\n                        <li><strong>loading="lazy"</strong> — Defers loading off-screen images</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Structured Data (Schema.org)</h2>\n                <p>Structured data helps search engines understand your content and can create rich snippets in search results.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- JSON-LD format (recommended by Google) --&gt;\n&lt;script type="application/ld+json"&gt;\n{\n  "@context": "https://schema.org",\n  "@type": "Recipe",\n  "name": "Chocolate Chip Cookies",\n  "description": "Easy homemade chocolate chip cookies",\n  "author": {\n    "@type": "Person",\n    "name": "Jane Baker"\n  },\n  "cookTime": "PT12M",\n  "recipeYield": "24 cookies",\n  "recipeIngredient": [\n    "2 cups flour",\n    "1 cup butter, softened",\n    "2 eggs"\n  ],\n  "recipeInstructions": [\n    "Preheat oven to 375°F",\n    "Mix butter and sugars until fluffy",\n    "Add eggs and vanilla"\n  ]\n}\n&lt;/script&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>What this creates:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>@type": "Recipe"</code> — Tells Google this is a recipe</li>\n                        <li>Enables rich results with cook time, ratings, and photos</li>\n                        <li>Other types: Article, Product, LocalBusiness, FAQ, HowTo</li>\n                        <li>Test with Google\'s Rich Results Test tool</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Meta Tags for SEO</h2>\n                <p>Additional meta tags provide information to search engines and social media platforms.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Robots meta tag --&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="robots" content="index, follow"&gt;\n  &lt;!-- index: allow search engines to index this page --&gt;\n  &lt;!-- follow: allow following links on this page --&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Canonical URL (prevents duplicate content issues) --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="canonical" href="https://example.com/blog/chocolate-cookies"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Open Graph (Facebook, LinkedIn, etc.) --&gt;\n  &lt;meta property="og:title" content="Best Chocolate Chip Cookies"&gt;\n  &lt;meta property="og:description" content="Easy recipe for perfect cookies"&gt;\n  &lt;meta property="og:image" content="https://example.com/cookies.jpg"&gt;\n  &lt;meta property="og:type" content="article"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Twitter Card --&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="twitter:title" content="Best Chocolate Chip Cookies"&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="twitter:description" content="Easy recipe for perfect cookies"&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="twitter:image" content="https://example.com/cookies.jpg"&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Meta tag purposes:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>robots</code> — Controls crawler behavior (index/noindex, follow/nofollow)</li>\n                        <li><code>canonical</code> — Specifies the preferred URL when duplicates exist</li>\n                        <li><code>og:*</code> — Controls how content appears when shared on social media</li>\n                        <li><code>twitter:*</code> — Twitter-specific card formatting</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. URL Structure</h2>\n                <p>Clean, descriptive URLs help both users and search engines understand your page content.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Bad URLs --&gt;\nhttps://example.com/p?id=123&amp;cat=5\nhttps://example.com/blog/post?a=1&amp;b=2&amp;c=3\nhttps://example.com/this-is-a-very-long-url-with-too-many-keywords-stuffed-into-it\n\n&lt;!-- Good URLs --&gt;\nhttps://example.com/products/running-shoes\nhttps://example.com/blog/how-to-bake-bread\nhttps://example.com/recipes/chocolate-chip-cookies\n\n&lt;!-- URL best practices --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Use words, not IDs --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Separate words with hyphens --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Keep URLs short and descriptive --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Use lowercase only --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Avoid special characters --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>9. Internal Linking</h2>\n                <p>Linking between your own pages helps search engines discover content and understand site structure.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Good internal linking --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Learn more about &lt;a href="/baking/bread-basics"&gt;bread baking basics&lt;/a&gt; \nbefore attempting this recipe. Check out our &lt;a href="/tips/kneading"&gt;kneading \ntips&lt;/a&gt; for better results.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Descriptive link text (not "click here") --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;For more information, &lt;a href="/guide"&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Read our complete &lt;a href="/guide"&gt;baking guide&lt;/a&gt; for more information.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Navigation with aria-current --&gt;\n&lt;nav&gt;\n  &lt;a href="/"&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;\n  &lt;a href="/blog" aria-current="page"&gt;Blog&lt;/a&gt;\n  &lt;a href="/about"&gt;About&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;/nav&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Internal linking best practices:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Descriptive anchor text:</strong> "bread baking basics" not "click here"</li>\n                        <li><strong>Relevant links:</strong> Link to related content</li>\n                        <li><strong>Reasonable number:</strong> Don\'t overload with links</li>\n                        <li><code>aria-current="page"</code> — Indicates current page in navigation</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>10. Mobile-First and Performance</h2>\n                <p>Google uses mobile-first indexing, meaning it primarily uses the mobile version of your site for ranking.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Essential for mobile --&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Preconnect to important third-party origins --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="preconnect" href="https://fonts.googleapis.com"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Preload critical resources --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="preload" href="critical.css" as="style"&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Performance tips --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Compress images (use WebP format when possible) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Minimize CSS and JavaScript --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Use lazy loading for images --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Enable browser caching --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ Use a Content Delivery Network (CDN) --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Core Web Vitals:</strong> Google\'s Core Web Vitals (LCP, INP, CLS) are ranking factors. Test your pages with PageSpeed Insights to ensure good performance scores.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Optimize this HTML for SEO:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Before: Poor SEO --&gt;\n&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;html&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;Page 1&lt;/title&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;div&gt;\n    &lt;div&gt;How to Cook Pasta&lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;img src="img001.jpg"&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Click &lt;a href="p2.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; for more.&lt;/p&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Try optimizing it yourself! --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Write unique, descriptive title tags (50-60 characters)</li>\n                    <li>Include meta descriptions for better click-through rates</li>\n                    <li>Use proper heading hierarchy (H1 → H2 → H3)</li>\n                    <li>Semantic HTML helps search engines understand content</li>\n                    <li>Optimize images with descriptive filenames and alt text</li>\n                    <li>Use structured data for rich search results</li>\n                    <li>Keep URLs clean and descriptive</li>\n                    <li>Link internally with descriptive anchor text</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson10.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: Accessibility</a>\n            <a href="lesson12.html" class="btn-primary">Next: Best Practices & Validation →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner. This lesson covers the essential best practices and validation techniques used by professional developers.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. Document Structure Best Practices</h2>\n                <p>Every HTML document should start with the proper structure.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;!-- \n  DOCTYPE declaration must be on the first line.\n  It triggers standards mode in browsers.\n--&gt;\n\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n&lt;!-- \n  lang attribute is required for accessibility.\n  It helps screen readers pronounce content correctly.\n  Use the appropriate language code: en, es, fr, de, etc.\n--&gt;\n\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Character encoding must be declared early --&gt;\n  &lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Viewport meta for responsive design --&gt;\n  &lt;meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Title is required in every document --&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;Page Title&lt;/title&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- CSS should be in the head for performance --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="styles.css"&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Page content goes here --&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Scripts at the end of body for performance --&gt;\n  &lt;script src="main.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Essential structure rules:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</code> — Must be first line, no exceptions</li>\n                        <li><code>lang="en"</code> — Required for accessibility and SEO</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;</code> — Should be first in head</li>\n                        <li><code>&lt;title&gt;</code> — Required, one per document</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. HTML Validation</h2>\n                <p>Validation checks your HTML against the official specification. The W3C Validator is the standard tool for this.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Common validation errors to avoid --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ERROR: Missing required attribute --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;img src="photo.jpg"&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;img src="photo.jpg" alt="Description of photo"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ERROR: Duplicate ID --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;div id="header"&gt;...&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;div id="header"&gt;...&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;div id="main-header"&gt;...&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;div id="mobile-header"&gt;...&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ERROR: Unclosed element --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;First paragraph\n&lt;p&gt;Second paragraph\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;First paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Second paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ERROR: Improper nesting --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Bold and italic&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Bold and italic&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ERROR: Block element inside inline --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;span&gt;\n  &lt;div&gt;This is invalid&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/span&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;div&gt;\n  &lt;span&gt;This is valid&lt;/span&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Validation Tools:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><a href="https://validator.w3.org/">W3C Markup Validator</a> — Official validator</li>\n                        <li>VS Code extensions like "HTMLHint" for real-time validation</li>\n                        <li>Browser DevTools can also show HTML parsing errors</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. Code Formatting and Readability</h2>\n                <p>Consistent formatting makes your code easier to read, understand, and maintain.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Bad: Hard to read --&gt;\n&lt;div class="container"&gt;&lt;div class="row"&gt;&lt;div class="col"&gt;&lt;p&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good: Properly indented --&gt;\n&lt;div class="container"&gt;\n  &lt;div class="row"&gt;\n    &lt;div class="col"&gt;\n      &lt;p&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Use consistent indentation (2 or 4 spaces) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Many developers use 2 spaces for HTML --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Align attributes for long elements --&gt;\n&lt;input type="text" \n       id="username" \n       name="username" \n       placeholder="Enter your username"\n       required&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Comment complex sections --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ====== Navigation Section ====== --&gt;\n&lt;nav aria-label="Main navigation"&gt;\n  &lt;ul&gt;\n    &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="/"&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n    &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="/about"&gt;About&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n  &lt;/ul&gt;\n&lt;/nav&gt;\n&lt;!-- ====== End Navigation ====== --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Formatting guidelines:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Indentation:</strong> Use 2 or 4 spaces consistently</li>\n                        <li><strong>Line length:</strong> Break long lines for readability</li>\n                        <li><strong>Comments:</strong> Document complex or non-obvious sections</li>\n                        <li><strong>Tools:</strong> Use Prettier or similar for automatic formatting</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Semantic Markup</h2>\n                <p>Use elements for their meaning, not their default appearance. This improves accessibility, SEO, and maintainability.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Bad: Using elements for styling --&gt;\n&lt;span style="font-size: 24px; font-weight: bold;"&gt;Heading&lt;/span&gt;\n&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;\n&lt;span style="font-size: 18px; font-weight: bold;"&gt;Subheading&lt;/span&gt;\n&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;\nThis is my paragraph text.\n\n&lt;!-- Good: Using semantic elements --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Heading&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h2&gt;Subheading&lt;/h2&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;This is my paragraph text.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Bad: Empty elements for spacing --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;First paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Second paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good: CSS for spacing --&gt;\n&lt;p class="mb-4"&gt;First paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Second paragraph&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;style&gt;\n  .mb-4 { margin-bottom: 1.5rem; }\n&lt;/style&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Why semantics matter:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Accessibility:</strong> Screen readers understand semantic elements</li>\n                        <li><strong>SEO:</strong> Search engines give weight to proper headings</li>\n                        <li><strong>Maintainability:</strong> Easier to understand and modify</li>\n                        <li><strong>Styling:</strong> Easier to style with CSS</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. ID vs Class Best Practices</h2>\n                <p>Understanding when to use IDs vs classes is fundamental to writing good HTML.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- ID: Unique identifier, use once per page --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good uses for IDs: --&gt;\n&lt;header id="site-header"&gt;...&lt;/header&gt;        &lt;!-- Landmark --&gt;\n&lt;main id="main-content"&gt;...&lt;/main&gt;          &lt;!-- Skip link target --&gt;\n&lt;form id="contact-form"&gt;...&lt;/form&gt;         &lt;!-- Form identification --&gt;\n&lt;input id="email" type="email"&gt;           &lt;!-- Label association --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Class: Reusable, can appear multiple times --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Good uses for classes: --&gt;\n&lt;article class="card"&gt;...&lt;/article&gt;        &lt;!-- Reusable component --&gt;\n&lt;article class="card"&gt;...&lt;/article&gt;        &lt;!-- Same class, different content --&gt;\n&lt;p class="text-center text-muted"&gt;...&lt;/p&gt; &lt;!-- Utility classes --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Multiple classes for composition --&gt;\n&lt;button class="btn btn-primary btn-large"&gt;\n  Submit\n&lt;/button&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Avoid using IDs for styling --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Bad --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  #main-button { background: purple; }\n&lt;/style&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Good --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  .btn-primary { background: purple; }\n&lt;/style&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>ID vs Class comparison:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>ID:</strong> Unique per page, use for anchors, form labels, JavaScript hooks</li>\n                        <li><strong>Class:</strong> Reusable, use for styling and grouping elements</li>\n                        <li><strong>Convention:</strong> IDs typically used for JavaScript, classes for CSS</li>\n                        <li><strong>Specificity:</strong> ID has higher specificity, can cause CSS issues</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Comments and Documentation</h2>\n                <p>Good comments help others (and your future self) understand your code.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Single-line comment --&gt;\n&lt;!-- This is a comment that explains the code below --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- \n  Multi-line comment\n  Useful for longer explanations or temporarily\n  commenting out code during debugging.\n--&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- TODO comments for future work --&gt;\n&lt;!-- TODO: Add responsive styles for mobile --&gt;\n&lt;!-- FIXME: This form validation needs improvement --&gt;\n&lt;!-- NOTE: This relies on JavaScript being enabled --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Closing tags with comments for long sections --&gt;\n&lt;div class="complex-component"&gt;\n  &lt;!-- ... hundreds of lines of code ... --&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;&lt;!-- /.complex-component --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Section markers --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ==================== HEADER ==================== --&gt;\n&lt;header&gt;\n  ...\n&lt;/header&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ==================== MAIN CONTENT ==================== --&gt;\n&lt;main&gt;\n  ...\n&lt;/main&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ==================== FOOTER ==================== --&gt;\n&lt;footer&gt;\n  ...\n&lt;/footer&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Performance Best Practices</h2>\n                <p>Write HTML that loads fast and renders efficiently.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Preload critical resources --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="preload" href="fonts/roboto.woff2" as="font" crossorigin&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Preconnect to external domains --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="preconnect" href="https://fonts.googleapis.com"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Async/defer for non-critical scripts --&gt;\n  &lt;script src="analytics.js" async&gt;&lt;/script&gt;\n  &lt;!-- async: Downloads in parallel, executes when ready --&gt;\n  \n  &lt;script src="app.js" defer&gt;&lt;/script&gt;\n  &lt;!-- defer: Downloads in parallel, executes after HTML parsed --&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Lazy load images below the fold --&gt;\n  &lt;img src="hero.jpg" alt="Hero image" width="800" height="400"&gt;\n  &lt;img src="gallery-1.jpg" alt="Gallery item" loading="lazy"&gt;\n  &lt;img src="gallery-2.jpg" alt="Gallery item" loading="lazy"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Always include width and height --&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Prevents Cumulative Layout Shift (CLS) --&gt;\n  &lt;img src="photo.jpg" alt="Photo" width="600" height="400"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Use modern image formats with fallback --&gt;\n  &lt;picture&gt;\n    &lt;source srcset="image.avif" type="image/avif"&gt;\n    &lt;source srcset="image.webp" type="image/webp"&gt;\n    &lt;img src="image.jpg" alt="Photo description"&gt;\n  &lt;/picture&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Performance tips:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>preload</code> — Load critical resources earlier</li>\n                        <li><code>preconnect</code> — Establish connections to external domains early</li>\n                        <li><code>async</code> — For independent scripts like analytics</li>\n                        <li><code>defer</code> — For scripts that need the DOM</li>\n                        <li><code>loading="lazy"</code> — Defer off-screen images</li>\n                        <li><code>width/height</code> — Prevent layout shift</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. Security Considerations</h2>\n                <p>HTML has built-in security features you should use.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Content Security Policy meta tag --&gt;\n  &lt;meta http-equiv="Content-Security-Policy" \n        content="default-src \'self\'; script-src \'self\' https://trusted.cdn.com"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Helps prevent XSS attacks by restricting resource sources --&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Use rel="noopener" for external links opened in new tabs --&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Prevents the new page from accessing window.opener --&gt;\n  &lt;a href="https://external-site.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;\n    External Link\n  &lt;/a&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Use rel="nofollow" for untrusted links --&gt;\n  &lt;a href="https://spam-site.com" rel="nofollow"&gt;\n    User-submitted Link\n  &lt;/a&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Disable autocomplete for sensitive fields --&gt;\n  &lt;input type="password" name="password" autocomplete="new-password"&gt;\n  &lt;input type="credit-card" name="cc" autocomplete="off"&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Use input types for built-in validation --&gt;\n  &lt;input type="email" name="email" required&gt;\n  &lt;!-- Browser validates email format before submission --&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Security checklist:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Always use <code>rel="noopener"</code> with <code>target="_blank"</code></li>\n                        <li>Consider CSP headers to prevent XSS</li>\n                        <li>Never trust user input — always sanitize on the server</li>\n                        <li>Use HTTPS for all resources</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>9. Common Mistakes to Avoid</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- ❌ MISTAKE: Inline styles everywhere --&gt;\n&lt;p style="color: red; font-size: 14px;"&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ BETTER: Use classes with CSS --&gt;\n&lt;p class="error-text"&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ❌ MISTAKE: Using tables for layout --&gt;\n&lt;table&gt;\n  &lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;Header&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;\n  &lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;Content&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;\n&lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ BETTER: Use semantic elements --&gt;\n&lt;header&gt;Header&lt;/header&gt;\n&lt;main&gt;Content&lt;/main&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ❌ MISTAKE: Skipping heading levels --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Title&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h3&gt;Subtitle&lt;/h3&gt;  &lt;!-- Skipped h2! --&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ BETTER: Proper hierarchy --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Title&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h2&gt;Subtitle&lt;/h2&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ❌ MISTAKE: Empty links or buttons --&gt;\n&lt;a href="#"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ BETTER: Provide accessible text --&gt;\n&lt;a href="#section"&gt;Skip to section&lt;/a&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ❌ MISTAKE: Multiple h1 elements --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;First heading&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Second heading&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;!-- ✓ BETTER: One h1 per page --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Main heading&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h2&gt;Section heading&lt;/h2&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>10. HTML Validation Checklist</h2>\n                <p>Before publishing any page, verify these items:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- ✓ DOCTYPE declaration present --&gt;\n&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Language attribute set --&gt;\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Character encoding declared --&gt;\n&lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Viewport meta for responsive --&gt;\n&lt;meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Unique page title --&gt;\n&lt;title&gt;Page Title | Site Name&lt;/title&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ All images have alt text --&gt;\n&lt;img src="image.jpg" alt="Description"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ All form inputs have labels --&gt;\n&lt;label for="email"&gt;Email&lt;/label&gt;\n&lt;input type="email" id="email"&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ IDs are unique --&gt;\n&lt;div id="unique-id-1"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;div id="unique-id-2"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Proper heading hierarchy --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Main&lt;/h1&gt; → &lt;h2&gt;Section&lt;/h2&gt; → &lt;h3&gt;Subsection&lt;/h3&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ All elements properly closed --&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- ✓ Valid nesting --&gt;\n&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;text&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Final Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Fix all the issues in this poorly written HTML:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Fix all the problems in this code --&gt;\n&lt;html&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n&lt;title&gt;my page&lt;/title&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n&lt;body&gt;\n&lt;div id="header"&gt;\n  &lt;div id="header"&gt;\n    &lt;span style="font-size: 24px"&gt;Welcome&lt;/span&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;img src="banner.jpg"&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Main Title&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;h3&gt;Subtitle&lt;/h3&gt;\n&lt;a href="http://external.com" target="_blank"&gt;Visit&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;form&gt;\n  &lt;input type="text" placeholder="Name"&gt;\n&lt;/form&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Always include DOCTYPE, lang, charset, viewport, and title</li>\n                    <li>Validate your HTML with the W3C Validator</li>\n                    <li>Use semantic elements for their meaning, not appearance</li>\n                    <li>Write clean, well-indented, commented code</li>\n                    <li>Use IDs for unique elements, classes for reusable styles</li>\n                    <li>Include width/height on images for performance</li>\n                    <li>Use async/defer for scripts to improve load times</li>\n                    <li>Always consider accessibility and security</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="conclusion">\n                <h2>🎉 Congratulations!</h2>\n                <p>You\'ve completed the HTML Course! You now have a solid foundation in HTML from beginner concepts like document structure and text elements to pro-level skills like accessibility, SEO, and best practices. The skills you\'ve learned here will serve as the foundation for learning CSS and JavaScript.</p>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>What\'s next?</strong>\n                    <p>Continue your learning journey with the <strong>CSS Course</strong> to learn how to style your HTML documents and create beautiful, responsive designs.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson11.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: SEO Best Practices</a>\n            <a href="../../index.html" class="btn-primary">Back to Dashboard →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner.
