{'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="courses/css/lesson1.html">\n<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang="en">\n<head>\n    <meta charset="UTF-8">\n    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">\n    <title>Lesson 1: Introduction to CSS - Learner</title>\n    <link rel="stylesheet" href="../../css/styles.css">\n</head>\n<body>\n    <header>\n        <div class="header-content">\n            <h1 class="logo">Learner</h1>\n            <nav>\n                <a href="../../index.html">Home</a>\n                <a href="index.html">CSS Course</a>\n            </nav>\n        </div>\n    </header>\n    \n    <main>\n        <div class="lesson-header">\n            <span class="lesson-badge">Beginner Level</span>\n            <h1>Lesson 1: Introduction to CSS</h1>\n            <p>Understanding what CSS is and how it styles the web</p>\n            <div class="progress-bar">\n                <div class="progress" style="width: 8%;"></div>\n            </div>\n            <span class="progress-text">Lesson 1 of 12</span>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-content">\n            <section class="intro">\n                <h2>What is CSS?</h2>\n                <p>CSS (Cascading Style Sheets) is the language used to style and layout web pages. While HTML provides the structure and content, CSS controls how that content looks — colors, fonts, spacing, layouts, and even animations. Think of HTML as the skeleton of a webpage and CSS as the skin and clothing that makes it look good.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>CSS vs HTML: Understanding the Difference</h2>\n                <p>HTML and CSS work together but serve different purposes:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- HTML: Structure and Content --&gt;\n&lt;h1&gt;Welcome to My Website&lt;/h1&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;This is a paragraph of text.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;button&gt;Click Me&lt;/button&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- CSS: Presentation and Style --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  h1 {\n    color: purple;\n    font-size: 32px;\n  }\n  \n  p {\n    color: gray;\n    line-height: 1.6;\n  }\n  \n  button {\n    background-color: #7C3AED;\n    color: white;\n    padding: 10px 20px;\n    border: none;\n    border-radius: 5px;\n  }\n&lt;/style&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>HTML does:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Define what elements are on the page (headings, paragraphs, buttons)</li>\n                        <li>Provide structure and meaning (semantics)</li>\n                        <li>Contain the actual content (text, images)</li>\n                    </ul>\n                    <strong>CSS does:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Control visual appearance (colors, fonts, sizes)</li>\n                        <li>Manage layout and positioning</li>\n                        <li>Add visual effects (shadows, animations)</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>The Three Ways to Add CSS</h2>\n                <p>There are three methods to apply CSS to your HTML, each with different use cases.</p>\n                \n                <h3>1. Inline CSS</h3>\n                <p>Write CSS directly in an HTML element\'s style attribute. Use this sparingly — it\'s hard to maintain.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Inline CSS: Styles directly on the element --&gt;\n&lt;p style="color: purple; font-size: 18px;"&gt;\n  This paragraph has inline styles.\n&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;button style="background: purple; color: white; padding: 10px;"&gt;\n  Styled Button\n&lt;/button&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Line by line:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>style="..."</code> — The style attribute holds CSS declarations</li>\n                        <li><code>color: purple;</code> — Sets text color to purple</li>\n                        <li><code>font-size: 18px;</code> — Sets text size to 18 pixels</li>\n                        <li>Multiple declarations separated by semicolons</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>When to use inline CSS:</strong> Quick tests, email HTML, dynamic styles from JavaScript. Avoid for regular styling — it\'s hard to maintain and override.\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>2. Internal CSS</h3>\n                <p>Write CSS inside a &lt;style&gt; tag in the HTML document\'s head. Good for single-page styles.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;My Page&lt;/title&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Internal CSS: Styles for this page only --&gt;\n  &lt;style&gt;\n    body {\n      background-color: #f5f5f5;\n      font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\n    }\n    \n    h1 {\n      color: #7C3AED;\n      text-align: center;\n    }\n    \n    .highlight {\n      background-color: yellow;\n      padding: 2px 5px;\n    }\n  &lt;/style&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;h1&gt;Welcome&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;This is &lt;span class="highlight"&gt;highlighted text&lt;/span&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Line by line:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;style&gt;</code> — Contains CSS rules for this document</li>\n                        <li><code>body { ... }</code> — Selects the body element</li>\n                        <li><code>background-color: #f5f5f5;</code> — Light gray background</li>\n                        <li><code>.highlight { ... }</code> — Selects elements with class "highlight"</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>3. External CSS (Recommended)</h3>\n                <p>Write CSS in a separate .css file and link it. This is the best practice for most projects.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- HTML file (index.html) --&gt;\n&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;My Page&lt;/title&gt;\n  \n  &lt;!-- Link to external stylesheet --&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="styles.css"&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;h1&gt;Welcome&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;p class="intro"&gt;Hello, world!&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* CSS file (styles.css) */\n/* This is a separate file containing all styles */\n\nbody {\n  background-color: white;\n  font-family: \'Segoe UI\', Arial, sans-serif;\n  margin: 0;\n  padding: 20px;\n}\n\nh1 {\n  color: #7C3AED;\n  font-size: 2.5rem;\n}\n\n.intro {\n  color: #666;\n  font-size: 1.1rem;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Line by line:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>&lt;link rel="stylesheet"&gt;</code> — Tells browser this is a stylesheet</li>\n                        <li><code>href="styles.css"</code> — Path to the CSS file</li>\n                        <li><code>/* comment */</code> — CSS comments (not visible in browser)</li>\n                        <li>Each rule follows: selector { property: value; }</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Why external CSS is best:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Separation of concerns (HTML for structure, CSS for style)</li>\n                        <li>One CSS file can style multiple HTML pages</li>\n                        <li>Browsers cache CSS files for faster loading</li>\n                        <li>Easier to maintain and collaborate on</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>CSS Syntax Explained</h2>\n                <p>Understanding the basic building blocks of CSS rules.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* CSS Rule Structure */\nselector {\n  property: value;\n  another-property: another-value;\n}\n\n/* Real Example */\nh1 {\n  color: purple;\n  font-size: 24px;\n  margin-bottom: 10px;\n}\n\n/* Breaking it down: */\n/*\n  h1        → Selector (what to style)\n  { }       → Declaration block (contains all styles)\n  color     → Property name (what aspect to change)\n  purple    → Property value (how to change it)\n  ;         → Semicolon (ends each declaration)\n*/</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>CSS terminology:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Selector:</strong> Points to the HTML element(s) to style</li>\n                        <li><strong>Declaration block:</strong> Contains one or more declarations</li>\n                        <li><strong>Declaration:</strong> A property-value pair</li>\n                        <li><strong>Property:</strong> The aspect to style (color, size, margin)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Value:</strong> The setting for that property</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>Cascading: The "C" in CSS</h2>\n                <p>The "Cascading" part means styles can come from multiple sources and the browser determines which styles win.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Multiple sources of styles --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- 1. Browser defaults (user agent stylesheet) --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Every browser has default styles for elements --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- 2. External CSS --&gt;\n&lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="styles.css"&gt;\n&lt;!-- styles.css: p { color: blue; } --&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- 3. Internal CSS --&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n  p { color: green; }\n&lt;/style&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- 4. Inline CSS --&gt;\n&lt;p style="color: red;"&gt;What color am I?&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;!-- Result: Red! Inline has highest priority --&gt;\n&lt;!-- Priority: Inline > Internal > External > Browser defaults --&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Cascade order (lowest to highest priority):</strong>\n                    <ol>\n                        <li><strong>Browser defaults:</strong> Built-in styles</li>\n                        <li><strong>External CSS:</strong> Linked stylesheets</li>\n                        <li><strong>Internal CSS:</strong> Style tags in head</li>\n                        <li><strong>Inline CSS:</strong> Style attribute on element</li>\n                        <li><strong>!important:</strong> Overrides everything (use sparingly!)</li>\n                    </ol>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>Your First CSS Styles</h2>\n                <p>Let\'s write some basic CSS to style a simple webpage:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* styles.css - Your first stylesheet */\n\n/* Style the whole page */\nbody {\n  background-color: #ffffff;        /* White background */\n  color: #333333;                   /* Dark gray text */\n  font-family: Arial, sans-serif;   /* Clean, readable font */\n  margin: 0;                        /* Remove default margin */\n  padding: 20px;                    /* Add space inside */\n}\n\n/* Style headings */\nh1 {\n  color: #7C3AED;                   /* Purple color */\n  font-size: 32px;                  /* Larger text */\n  margin-bottom: 10px;              /* Space below */\n}\n\nh2 {\n  color: #9333EA;                   /* Darker purple */\n  font-size: 24px;\n}\n\n/* Style paragraphs */\np {\n  font-size: 16px;\n  line-height: 1.6;                 /* Better readability */\n  margin-bottom: 15px;\n}\n\n/* Style links */\na {\n  color: #7C3AED;\n  text-decoration: none;            /* Remove underline */\n}\n\na:hover {\n  text-decoration: underline;       /* Underline on hover */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Common CSS properties used:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>background-color</code> — Background color of element</li>\n                        <li><code>color</code> — Text color</li>\n                        <li><code>font-family</code> — Type of font</li>\n                        <li><code>font-size</code> — Size of text</li>\n                        <li><code>margin</code> — Space outside element</li>\n                        <li><code>padding</code> — Space inside element</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Create a simple HTML page and style it with an external CSS file:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;!-- Create index.html --&gt;\n&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;\n&lt;html lang="en"&gt;\n&lt;head&gt;\n  &lt;meta charset="UTF-8"&gt;\n  &lt;title&gt;My First Styled Page&lt;/title&gt;\n  &lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="styles.css"&gt;\n&lt;/head&gt;\n&lt;body&gt;\n  &lt;h1&gt;Hello, CSS!&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;This is my first styled paragraph.&lt;/p&gt;\n  &lt;a href="#"&gt;Click me&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;\n\n/* Create styles.css */\n/* Try styling: */\n/* - Purple background for the body */\n/* - White text for the heading */\n/* - Yellow links */\n/* - Large font size for the paragraph */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>CSS (Cascading Style Sheets) controls how HTML looks</li>\n                    <li>Three ways to add CSS: inline, internal, external (recommended)</li>\n                    <li>CSS syntax: selector { property: value; }</li>\n                    <li>The cascade determines which styles take priority</li>\n                    <li>External CSS is best for maintainability and caching</li>\n                    <li>Always use semicolons after each declaration</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="index.html" class="btn-secondary">← Course Overview</a>\n            <a href="lesson2.html" class="btn-primary">Next: Selectors →</a>\n        </div>\n Without selectors, CSS wouldn\'t know what to apply styles to. Mastering selectors is essential for writing efficient, targeted CSS. Think of selectors as the "address" that tells CSS where to deliver the styles.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. Element (Type) Selectors</h2>\n                <p>The simplest selector — targets all elements of a specific type.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Element Selector: targets all paragraphs */\np {\n  color: #333;\n  line-height: 1.6;\n}\n\n/* Targets all headings */\nh1 {\n  font-size: 32px;\n  color: #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Targets all links */\na {\n  color: purple;\n  text-decoration: none;\n}\n\n/* Targets all images */\nimg {\n  max-width: 100%;\n  height: auto;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>How it works:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Use the HTML tag name without brackets: <code>p</code>, <code>h1</code>, <code>div</code></li>\n                        <li>Styles apply to ALL elements of that type on the page</li>\n                        <li>Good for base styles that should be consistent</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. Class Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target elements with a specific class attribute. Classes are the most versatile selectors.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* HTML */\n&lt;p class="highlight"&gt;This paragraph is highlighted.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;This paragraph is normal.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;p class="highlight"&gt;Another highlighted paragraph.&lt;/p&gt;\n\n/* CSS */\n/* Class selector uses a dot (.) before the class name */\n.highlight {\n  background-color: yellow;\n  padding: 2px 5px;\n}\n\n/* Multiple classes on one element */\n&lt;button class="btn btn-primary btn-large"&gt;Submit&lt;/button&gt;\n\n/* Target specific combination */\n.btn-primary {\n  background-color: #7C3AED;\n  color: white;\n}\n\n.btn-large {\n  padding: 15px 30px;\n  font-size: 18px;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Class selector rules:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Syntax:</strong> Dot followed by class name: <code>.classname</code></li>\n                        <li><strong>Reusable:</strong> Same class can be used on multiple elements</li>\n                        <li><strong>Multiple classes:</strong> Elements can have multiple classes (space-separated)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Naming:</strong> Use lowercase, hyphens for spaces: <code>.btn-primary</code></li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Class naming best practices:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Use descriptive names: <code>.error-message</code> not <code>.red-text</code></li>\n                        <li>Use lowercase with hyphens: <code>.nav-link</code></li>\n                        <li>Avoid starting with numbers: <code>.1button</code> is invalid</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. ID Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target a single element with a unique ID. IDs should be unique per page.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* HTML */\n&lt;header id="main-header"&gt;\n  &lt;nav id="primary-nav"&gt;...&lt;/nav&gt;\n&lt;/header&gt;\n\n&lt;main id="content"&gt;\n  &lt;article id="featured-post"&gt;...&lt;/article&gt;\n&lt;/main&gt;\n\n/* CSS */\n/* ID selector uses a hash (#) before the ID name */\n#main-header {\n  background-color: #7C3AED;\n  padding: 20px;\n  position: sticky;\n  top: 0;\n}\n\n#primary-nav {\n  display: flex;\n  gap: 20px;\n}\n\n#featured-post {\n  border: 2px solid #7C3AED;\n  padding: 20px;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>ID selector characteristics:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Syntax:</strong> Hash followed by ID name: <code>#idname</code></li>\n                        <li><strong>Unique:</strong> Only one element per page should have each ID</li>\n                        <li><strong>High specificity:</strong> ID selectors override class selectors</li>\n                        <li><strong>Use for:</strong> Landmarks, skip link targets, JavaScript hooks</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>ID vs Class:</strong> Prefer classes for styling. IDs are better for JavaScript and page landmarks. ID\'s high specificity can make CSS harder to maintain.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Attribute Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target elements based on their attributes or attribute values.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Target elements with a specific attribute */\n[disabled] {\n  opacity: 0.5;\n  cursor: not-allowed;\n}\n\n/* Target elements with specific attribute value */\n[type="email"] {\n  background-image: url(\'email-icon.svg\');\n  background-position: right 10px center;\n  background-repeat: no-repeat;\n}\n\n[type="password"] {\n  letter-spacing: 2px;\n}\n\n/* Target links that start with "https" */\n[href^="https"] {\n  color: green;\n}\n\n/* Target links ending with ".pdf" */\n[href$=".pdf"] {\n  padding-right: 20px;\n  background-image: url(\'pdf-icon.svg\');\n  background-repeat: no-repeat;\n}\n\n/* Target links containing "example" */\n[href*="example"] {\n  font-weight: bold;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Attribute selector patterns:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>[attr]</code> — Has the attribute</li>\n                        <li><code>[attr="value"]</code> — Attribute equals value exactly</li>\n                        <li><code>[attr^="value"]</code> — Attribute starts with value</li>\n                        <li><code>[attr$="value"]</code> — Attribute ends with value</li>\n                        <li><code>[attr*="value"]</code> — Attribute contains value</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. Descendant and Child Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target elements based on their relationship to other elements.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* HTML structure */\n&lt;nav class="main-nav"&gt;\n  &lt;ul&gt;\n    &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="#"&gt;Home&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n    &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="#"&gt;About&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n  &lt;/ul&gt;\n&lt;/nav&gt;\n\n&lt;article&gt;\n  &lt;p&gt;Paragraph with &lt;a href="#"&gt;a link&lt;/a&gt; inside.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/article&gt;\n\n/* Descendant selector (space) - any nested element */\n.main-nav a {\n  color: white;\n  text-decoration: none;\n}\n/* Targets ALL links inside .main-nav, at any depth */\n\n/* Child selector (>) - direct children only */\n.main-nav > ul {\n  list-style: none;\n}\n/* Targets only ul that is a DIRECT child of .main-nav */\n\n/* Combined selectors */\narticle p a {\n  color: #7C3AED;\n  border-bottom: 1px dotted #7C3AED;\n}\n/* Links inside paragraphs inside articles */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Combinator comparison:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>.parent .child</code> (space) — Any descendant at any level</li>\n                        <li><code>.parent > .child</code> — Direct child only</li>\n                        <li>Descendant is more flexible but can be slower</li>\n                        <li>Child is more specific and performs better</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Pseudo-Class Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target elements based on state or position. Use a single colon (:).</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Mouse interaction states */\na:link {\n  color: blue;              /* Unvisited link */\n}\n\na:visited {\n  color: purple;            /* Visited link */\n}\n\na:hover {\n  color: #7C3AED;           /* Mouse over */\n  text-decoration: underline;\n}\n\na:active {\n  color: red;               /* Being clicked */\n}\n\na:focus {\n  outline: 2px solid #7C3AED; /* Keyboard focus */\n}\n\n/* Form states */\ninput:focus {\n  border-color: #7C3AED;\n  box-shadow: 0 0 5px rgba(124, 58, 237, 0.3);\n}\n\ninput:disabled {\n  background-color: #f0f0f0;\n  cursor: not-allowed;\n}\n\ninput:valid {\n  border-color: green;\n}\n\ninput:invalid {\n  border-color: red;\n}\n\n/* Position-based */\nli:first-child {\n  font-weight: bold;\n}\n\nli:last-child {\n  border-bottom: none;\n}\n\nli:nth-child(odd) {\n  background-color: #f9f9f9;\n}\n\nli:nth-child(3) {\n  color: purple;            /* Third item only */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Common pseudo-classes:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>:hover</code> — Mouse is over element</li>\n                        <li><code>:focus</code> — Element has keyboard focus</li>\n                        <li><code>:active</code> — Element is being activated (clicked)</li>\n                        <li><code>:first-child</code> — First element among siblings</li>\n                        <li><code>:last-child</code> — Last element among siblings</li>\n                        <li><code>:nth-child(n)</code> — nth element (odd, even, 3, 2n+1)</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Pseudo-Element Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Target specific parts of an element. Use double colon (::).</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* First letter of text */\np::first-letter {\n  font-size: 2em;\n  font-weight: bold;\n  color: #7C3AED;\n  float: left;\n  margin-right: 5px;\n}\n\n/* First line of text */\np::first-line {\n  font-weight: bold;\n  color: #333;\n}\n\n/* Insert content before an element */\n.required::before {\n  content: "* ";\n  color: red;\n}\n\n/* Insert content after an element */\n.new-link::after {\n  content: " (new)";\n  color: #7C3AED;\n  font-size: 0.8em;\n}\n\n/* Style placeholder text */\ninput::placeholder {\n  color: #999;\n  font-style: italic;\n}\n\n/* Style selected text */\n::selection {\n  background-color: #7C3AED;\n  color: white;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Pseudo-element uses:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>::before</code> / <code>::after</code> — Add decorative content</li>\n                        <li><code>::first-letter</code> — Drop caps, styling initials</li>\n                        <li><code>::first-line</code> — Style first line differently</li>\n                        <li><code>::placeholder</code> — Style form placeholders</li>\n                        <li><code>::selection</code> — Style highlighted text</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. Grouping Selectors</h2>\n                <p>Apply the same styles to multiple selectors using commas.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Group multiple selectors with commas */\nh1, h2, h3, h4, h5, h6 {\n  color: #333;\n  font-family: \'Georgia\', serif;\n  margin-top: 0;\n}\n\n/* Mix different selector types */\n.highlight, .featured, #top-story {\n  border-left: 4px solid #7C3AED;\n  padding-left: 15px;\n}\n\n/* Group pseudo-classes */\na:hover, a:focus {\n  color: #9333EA;\n  text-decoration: underline;\n}\n\n/* Combine with descendant selectors */\n.main-nav a, .footer-nav a, .sidebar a {\n  text-decoration: none;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Tip:</strong> Grouping selectors reduces code duplication and keeps your CSS DRY (Don\'t Repeat Yourself).\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>9. Specificity: Which Selector Wins?</h2>\n                <p>When multiple selectors target the same element, specificity determines which styles apply.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Specificity ranking (lowest to highest): */\n\n/* 1. Element selectors (specificity: 0-0-1) */\np { color: black; }\n\n/* 2. Class selectors (specificity: 0-1-0) */\n.text { color: blue; }\n\n/* 3. ID selectors (specificity: 1-0-0) */\n#intro { color: green; }\n\n/* 4. Inline styles (specificity: 1-0-0-0) */\n&lt;p style="color: red;"&gt;Text&lt;/p&gt;\n\n/* Calculating specificity */\np { }                    /* 0-0-1 = 1 point */\n.text { }                /* 0-1-0 = 10 points */\np.text { }               /* 0-1-1 = 11 points */\n#intro { }               /* 1-0-0 = 100 points */\n#intro.text { }          /* 1-1-0 = 110 points */\n\n/* Example conflict */\np { color: black; }      /* Loses to class */\n.text { color: blue; }   /* Wins */\n&lt;p class="text"&gt;I\'m blue!&lt;/p&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Specificity rules:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Inline styles beat ID selectors</li>\n                        <li>ID selectors beat class selectors</li>\n                        <li>Class selectors beat element selectors</li>\n                        <li>More specific selectors override less specific ones</li>\n                        <li>When equal specificity, last declared wins</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Write selectors for these scenarios:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Challenge: Write selectors for: */\n\n/* 1. All paragraphs on the page */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 2. Elements with class "button" */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 3. The element with id "header" */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 4. Links inside the navigation */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 5. The first item in a list */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 6. Links when mouse hovers */\n/* Your selector: */\n\n/* 7. All h1, h2, and h3 headings */\n/* Your selector: */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Element selectors target all elements of a type (p, h1, div)</li>\n                    <li>Class selectors (.class) are reusable and versatile</li>\n                    <li>ID selectors (#id) should be unique per page</li>\n                    <li>Attribute selectors target elements by attributes</li>\n                    <li>Descendant (space) and child (>) selectors target nested elements</li>\n                    <li>Pseudo-classes (:) target states (:hover, :focus)</li>\n                    <li>Pseudo-elements (::) target parts of elements (::before, ::after)</li>\n                    <li>Specificity determines which styles win when conflicts occur</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson1.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: Introduction to CSS</a>\n            <a href="lesson3.html" class="btn-primary">Next: Colors and Text →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner. They set the mood, improve readability, and create visual hierarchy. This lesson covers all the ways to specify colors and control text appearance in CSS.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. Color Formats in CSS</h2>\n                <p>CSS provides multiple ways to specify colors. Understanding each format gives you flexibility and control.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Named Colors</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* CSS has 147 named colors */\np {\n  color: red;\n  color: blue;\n  color: purple;\n  color: crimson;\n  color: tomato;\n  color: steelblue;\n  color: mediumseagreen;\n}\n\n/* Common named colors */\n/* red, orange, yellow, green, blue, purple */\n/* black, white, gray, silver */\n/* transparent (fully transparent) */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Hexadecimal (Hex) Colors</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Hex format: #RRGGBB (Red, Green, Blue) */\nh1 {\n  color: #7C3AED;    /* Purple */\n}\n\n/* Two characters per color channel (00 to FF) */\n/* 00 = 0 (none), FF = 255 (full) */\n\n/* #RRGGBBAA - includes alpha (opacity) */\n.overlay {\n  background-color: #00000080;  /* Black at 50% opacity */\n}\n\n/* Shorthand: #RGB when pairs repeat */\np {\n  color: #333;       /* Same as #333333 */\n  color: #FFF;       /* Same as #FFFFFF */\n  color: #7A3;       /* Same as #77AA33 */\n}\n\n/* Shorthand with alpha: #RGBA */\n.box {\n  background-color: #0008;  /* Black at 50% opacity */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Understanding hex:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>#RRGGBB</code> — Six characters: Red, Green, Blue values</li>\n                        <li><code>00</code> = none, <code>FF</code> = maximum</li>\n                        <li><code>#7C3AED</code> — 7C (red), 3A (green), ED (blue) = purple</li>\n                        <li>Add two more characters for opacity: <code>#RRGGBBAA</code></li>\n                      </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>RGB and RGBA</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* RGB format: rgb(red, green, blue) */\n/* Values: 0-255 for each channel */\n\nh1 {\n  color: rgb(124, 58, 237);     /* Purple */\n}\n\n/* RGBA adds alpha (opacity): 0 (transparent) to 1 (opaque) */\n.overlay {\n  background-color: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.5);    /* Black, 50% transparent */\n}\n\n.button {\n  background-color: rgba(124, 58, 237, 0.8);  /* Purple, 80% opaque */\n}\n\n/* Useful for overlays and hover effects */\n.card:hover {\n  background-color: rgba(124, 58, 237, 0.1);\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>HSL and HSLA</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* HSL: Hue, Saturation, Lightness */\n/* More intuitive for adjusting colors */\n\n/* Hue: 0-360 (color wheel position) */\n/*   0 = red, 120 = green, 240 = blue, 270 = purple */\n/* Saturation: 0-100% (gray to vivid) */\n/* Lightness: 0-100% (black to white) */\n\nh1 {\n  color: hsl(258, 83%, 58%);    /* Purple */\n}\n\n/* HSLA adds alpha */\n.overlay {\n  background-color: hsla(258, 83%, 58%, 0.5);\n}\n\n/* Easy to create variations */\n.primary { color: hsl(258, 83%, 58%); }      /* Base */\n.primary-light { color: hsl(258, 83%, 78%); } /* Lighter */\n.primary-dark { color: hsl(258, 83%, 38%); }  /* Darker */\n\n/* Easy to create grayscale */\n.gray-1 { color: hsl(0, 0%, 10%); }   /* Very dark gray */\n.gray-2 { color: hsl(0, 0%, 50%); }   /* Medium gray */\n.gray-3 { color: hsl(0, 0%, 90%); }   /* Light gray */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Why HSL is useful:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Hue:</strong> Position on color wheel (0-360°)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Saturation:</strong> How vivid the color is</li>\n                        <li><strong>Lightness:</strong> How light or dark</li>\n                        <li>Easy to create color variations by changing one value</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Which format to use?</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Hex:</strong> Most common, great for copying from design tools</li>\n                        <li><strong>RGB/RGBA:</strong> When you need transparency</li>\n                        <li><strong>HSL:</strong> When creating color variations or palettes</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. CSS Color Properties</h2>\n                <p>Several properties control colors in different contexts.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Text color */\np {\n  color: #333333;              /* Sets text color */\n}\n\n/* Background color */\nbody {\n  background-color: #ffffff;   /* Page background */\n}\n\n.header {\n  background-color: #7C3AED;   /* Element background */\n}\n\n/* Border color */\n.box {\n  border: 2px solid #7C3AED;   /* Border in one declaration */\n  /* OR */\n  border-width: 2px;\n  border-style: solid;\n  border-color: #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Accent color (form controls) */\ninput:focus {\n  accent-color: #7C3AED;       /* Checkbox, radio, range color */\n}\n\n/* Caret color (text cursor) */\ninput {\n  caret-color: #7C3AED;        /* Blinking cursor color */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. Typography Basics</h2>\n                <p>Good typography makes your content readable and visually appealing.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Font Family</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Set the font for text */\nbody {\n  /* List fonts in order of preference */\n  font-family: \'Segoe UI\', Arial, sans-serif;\n}\n\nh1 {\n  /* Serif fonts have decorative strokes */\n  font-family: \'Georgia\', \'Times New Roman\', serif;\n}\n\n.code {\n  /* Monospace fonts - each character same width */\n  font-family: \'Consolas\', \'Monaco\', monospace;\n}\n\n/* Generic font families (fallbacks): */\n/* serif - Times New Roman, Georgia */\n/* sans-serif - Arial, Helvetica, Verdana */\n/* monospace - Courier, Consolas */\n/* cursive - Decorative, script-like */\n/* fantasy - Decorative, playful */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Font stack explained:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Browser tries first font, falls back if not available</li>\n                        <li>Always end with a generic family (serif, sans-serif, monospace)</li>\n                        <li>Font names with spaces need quotes</li>\n                      </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Font Size</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Absolute sizes */\nh1 {\n  font-size: 32px;      /* Pixels - fixed size */\n  font-size: 2rem;      /* Relative to root (html) */\n  font-size: 2em;       /* Relative to parent element */\n  font-size: 200%;      /* Percentage of parent */\n}\n\n/* Relative sizes (recommended) */\np {\n  font-size: 1rem;      /* Base paragraph size */\n}\n\nsmall {\n  font-size: 0.875rem;  /* 14px if base is 16px */\n}\n\n/* Keywords */\n.large { font-size: large; }\n.medium { font-size: medium; }\n.small { font-size: small; }\n.x-small { font-size: x-small; }\n\n/* Viewport-based (responsive) */\n.hero-title {\n  font-size: 5vw;       /* 5% of viewport width */\n  /* Caution: Can become too small/large */\n}\n\n/* Best practice: Use clamp() for responsive text */\n.hero-title {\n  font-size: clamp(1.5rem, 4vw, 3rem);\n  /* Min: 1.5rem, Preferred: 4vw, Max: 3rem */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Font Weight</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Control how bold text appears */\np {\n  font-weight: normal;    /* 400 - default */\n  font-weight: bold;      /* 700 */\n}\n\n/* Numeric values (100-900) */\n.light { font-weight: 300; }\n.regular { font-weight: 400; }\n.medium { font-weight: 500; }\n.semibold { font-weight: 600; }\n.bold { font-weight: 700; }\n.extrabold { font-weight: 800; }\n\n/* Relative values */\np {\n  font-weight: normal;\n}\n\nstrong {\n  font-weight: bolder;    /* Bolder than parent */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Font Style</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Italic and oblique text */\np {\n  font-style: normal;     /* Upright text */\n}\n\nem, i {\n  font-style: italic;     /* Italic text */\n}\n\n.oblique {\n  font-style: oblique;    /* Slanted text */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Text Properties</h2>\n                <p>CSS provides many properties for fine-tuning text appearance.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Line Height - spacing between lines */\np {\n  line-height: 1.6;       /* Unitless: multiplied by font-size */\n  line-height: 24px;      /* Fixed value */\n  line-height: 150%;      /* Percentage */\n}\n\n/* Unitless is recommended - inherits better */\nbody {\n  line-height: 1.5;       /* Good for readability */\n}\n\n/* Text Alignment */\nh1 {\n  text-align: center;     /* Center the text */\n}\n\np {\n  text-align: left;       /* Left aligned (default for LTR) */\n  text-align: right;      /* Right aligned */\n  text-align: justify;    /* Full width, newspaper style */\n}\n\n/* Text Decoration */\na {\n  text-decoration: none;              /* Remove underline */\n}\n\na:hover {\n  text-decoration: underline;         /* Add underline */\n}\n\n.deleted {\n  text-decoration: line-through;      /* Strikethrough */\n}\n\n.fancy {\n  text-decoration: underline wavy purple;  /* Style, line style, color */\n}\n\n/* Text Transform */\nh1 {\n  text-transform: uppercase;    /* ALL CAPS */\n}\n\nh2 {\n  text-transform: lowercase;    /* all lowercase */\n}\n\n.title {\n  text-transform: capitalize;   /* First Letter Of Each Word */\n}\n\n/* Letter Spacing */\nh1 {\n  letter-spacing: 2px;          /* Spread out letters */\n}\n\n.condensed {\n  letter-spacing: -1px;         /* Tighter letters */\n}\n\n/* Word Spacing */\np {\n  word-spacing: 5px;            /* Space between words */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. Text Indent and Overflow</h2>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Text Indent - first line indent */\np {\n  text-indent: 2em;             /* Indent first line */\n}\n\n/* Text Overflow - handling overflow */\n.truncate {\n  white-space: nowrap;          /* Prevent wrapping */\n  overflow: hidden;             /* Hide overflow */\n  text-overflow: ellipsis;      /* Show ... for overflow */\n}\n\n/* Word Wrap and Break */\n.long-url {\n  word-wrap: break-word;        /* Break long words */\n  overflow-wrap: break-word;    /* Modern property */\n}\n\n.no-wrap {\n  white-space: nowrap;          /* Never wrap */\n}\n\n.pre {\n  white-space: pre;             /* Preserve spaces and line breaks */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Text Shadow</h2>\n                <p>Add shadows to text for visual effects.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* text-shadow: horizontal vertical blur color */\nh1 {\n  /* Simple shadow */\n  text-shadow: 2px 2px 4px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.3);\n  \n  /* Breakdown: */\n  /* 2px - horizontal offset (right) */\n  /* 2px - vertical offset (down) */\n  /* 4px - blur radius (softness) */\n  /* rgba(...) - shadow color */\n}\n\n/* Multiple shadows */\n.fancy {\n  text-shadow: \n    1px 1px 0 #fff,\n    2px 2px 0 #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Glow effect */\n.glow {\n  color: #fff;\n  text-shadow: 0 0 10px #7C3AED, 0 0 20px #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Embossed effect */\n.embossed {\n  color: #666;\n  text-shadow: 1px 1px 0 #fff, -1px -1px 0 #333;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Custom Fonts (Web Fonts)</h2>\n                <p>Use custom fonts beyond what\'s installed on users\' computers.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Using Google Fonts */\n/* Step 1: Add link in HTML head */\n&lt;link href="https://fonts.googleapis.com/css2?family=Roboto:wght@400;700&display=swap" rel="stylesheet"&gt;\n\n/* Step 2: Use in CSS */\nbody {\n  font-family: \'Roboto\', sans-serif;\n}\n\n/* Using @font-face (self-hosted) */\n@font-face {\n  font-family: \'CustomFont\';\n  src: url(\'fonts/custom-font.woff2\') format(\'woff2\'),\n       url(\'fonts/custom-font.woff\') format(\'woff\');\n  font-weight: normal;\n  font-style: normal;\n}\n\nh1 {\n  font-family: \'CustomFont\', serif;\n}\n\n/* Font-display options */\n@font-face {\n  font-family: \'MyFont\';\n  src: url(\'my-font.woff2\') format(\'woff2\');\n  font-display: swap;  /* Show fallback font immediately, swap when loaded */\n  /* Other options: auto, block, swap, fallback, optional */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Font performance tips:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Use <code>font-display: swap</code> to avoid invisible text</li>\n                        <li>Limit the number of font weights you load</li>\n                        <li>Preload critical fonts: <code>&lt;link rel="preload" href="font.woff2" as="font" crossorigin&gt;</code></li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. Creating a Typography Scale</h2>\n                <p>A consistent scale creates visual harmony.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Base styles */\n:root {\n  --font-size-base: 1rem;      /* 16px */\n  --line-height-base: 1.5;\n  --font-family-base: \'Segoe UI\', Arial, sans-serif;\n}\n\n/* Type scale (1.25 ratio) */\nh1 { font-size: 2.441rem; }    /* ~39px */\nh2 { font-size: 1.953rem; }    /* ~31px */\nh3 { font-size: 1.563rem; }    /* ~25px */\nh4 { font-size: 1.25rem; }     /* ~20px */\np  { font-size: 1rem; }        /* 16px */\nsmall { font-size: 0.8rem; }   /* ~13px */\n\n/* Using CSS custom properties */\n:root {\n  --text-xs: 0.75rem;\n  --text-sm: 0.875rem;\n  --text-base: 1rem;\n  --text-lg: 1.125rem;\n  --text-xl: 1.25rem;\n  --text-2xl: 1.5rem;\n  --text-3xl: 1.875rem;\n  --text-4xl: 2.25rem;\n}\n\n.heading-1 { font-size: var(--text-4xl); }\n.body-text { font-size: var(--text-base); }\n.small-text { font-size: var(--text-sm); }</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Create a styled text component:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Create these styles for a blog post: */\n\n/* 1. Body text: dark gray, 1rem, 1.6 line-height */\n/* 2. Headings: purple, bold */\n/* 3. Links: purple, no underline, underline on hover */\n/* 4. Blockquotes: italic, gray, left border purple */\n/* 5. Code: monospace, light gray background */\n\n/* Your CSS here: */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Color formats: named, hex (#RRGGBB), RGB, HSL</li>\n                    <li>Use HSL for easy color variations</li>\n                    <li>font-family uses fallback fonts ending with generic family</li>\n                    <li>Relative units (rem, em) are preferred for accessibility</li>\n                    <li>line-height improves readability (1.5-1.8 for body text)</li>\n                    <li>text-transform, text-decoration, letter-spacing fine-tune text</li>\n                    <li>Web fonts expand your typography options</li>\n                    <li>A consistent type scale creates visual harmony</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson2.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: Selectors</a>\n            <a href="lesson4.html" class="btn-primary">Next: Box Model →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner. {'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="courses/css/lesson4.html">\n<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang="en">\n<head>\n    <meta charset="UTF-8">\n    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">\n    <title>Lesson 4: Box Model - Learner</title>\n    <link rel="stylesheet" href="../../css/styles.css">\n</head>\n<body>\n    <header>\n        <div class="header-content">\n            <h1 class="logo">Learner</h1>\n            <nav>\n                <a href="../../index.html">Home</a>\n                <a href="index.html">CSS Course</a>\n            </nav>\n        </div>\n    </header>\n    \n    <main>\n        <div class="lesson-header">\n            <span class="lesson-badge">Beginner Level</span>\n            <h1>Lesson 4: Box Model</h1>\n            <p>Understanding how CSS treats every element as a box</p>\n            <div class="progress-bar">\n                <div class="progress" style="width: 33%;"></div>\n            </div>\n            <span class="progress-text">Lesson 4 of 12</span>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-content">\n            <section class="intro">\n                <h2>The CSS Box Model</h2>\n                <p>In CSS, every element is treated as a rectangular box. Understanding the box model is essential for controlling layout, spacing, and sizing. The box model consists of four areas: content, padding, border, and margin. These layers determine how much space an element takes up and how it relates to other elements.</p>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>The Four Layers of the Box Model</h2>\n                <p>Every element box has four concentric layers:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Box Model Visualization */\n/*\n┌─────────────────────────────────────┐\n│              MARGIN                 │  ← Outermost: Space outside\n│   ┌─────────────────────────────┐   │\n│   │           BORDER            │   │  ← The border edge\n│   │   ┌─────────────────────┐   │   │\n│   │   │      PADDING        │   │   │  ← Space inside border\n│   │   │   ┌─────────────┐   │   │   │\n│   │   │   │   CONTENT   │   │   │   │  ← The actual content\n│   │   │   └─────────────┘   │   │   │\n│   │   └─────────────────────┘   │   │\n│   └─────────────────────────────┘   │\n└─────────────────────────────────────┘\n*/</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>The four layers:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Content:</strong> The actual content (text, images)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Padding:</strong> Space between content and border</li>\n                        <li><strong>Border:</strong> The edge around the padding</li>\n                        <li><strong>Margin:</strong> Space outside the border, between elements</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>1. Content Area</h2>\n                <p>The content area holds the element\'s actual content — text, images, or child elements.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Width and Height control the content area */\n.box {\n  width: 300px;           /* Content width */\n  height: 200px;          /* Content height */\n}\n\n/* Min and Max dimensions */\n.responsive {\n  width: 100%;\n  max-width: 1200px;      /* Won\'t exceed 1200px */\n  min-width: 300px;       /* Won\'t go below 300px */\n}\n\n.sidebar {\n  width: 250px;\n  min-height: 100vh;      /* At least full viewport height */\n}\n\n/* Intrinsic sizing keywords */\n.element {\n  width: fit-content;     /* Only as wide as content needs */\n  width: min-content;     /* As narrow as possible */\n  width: max-content;     /* As wide as content wants */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Width keywords:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>auto</code> — Default, fills available space</li>\n                        <li><code>fit-content</code> — Shrinks to fit content</li>\n                        <li><code>min-content</code> — Minimum width of content</li>\n                        <li><code>max-content</code> — Maximum width of content</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>2. Padding</h2>\n                <p>Padding creates space between the content and the border. It\'s inside the element and inherits the element\'s background.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Padding - space inside the border */\n.box {\n  /* All sides equal */\n  padding: 20px;\n}\n\n/* Different sides: top right bottom left (clockwise) */\n.card {\n  padding: 10px 20px 15px 25px;\n  /*       top  right bottom left */\n}\n\n/* Three values: top, right/left, bottom */\n.element {\n  padding: 10px 20px 15px;\n  /*       top  sides  bottom */\n}\n\n/* Two values: top/bottom, right/left */\n.section {\n  padding: 20px 40px;\n  /*       vertical horizontal */\n}\n\n/* Individual sides */\n.custom {\n  padding-top: 10px;\n  padding-right: 20px;\n  padding-bottom: 10px;\n  padding-left: 20px;\n}\n\n/* Inline shorthand */\n.inline-padding {\n  padding-inline: 20px;      /* Left and right in LTR */\n  padding-block: 10px;       /* Top and bottom */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Padding shorthand patterns:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>padding: 20px;</code> — All four sides</li>\n                        <li><code>padding: 10px 20px;</code> — Vertical | Horizontal</li>\n                        <li><code>padding: 10px 20px 15px;</code> — Top | Sides | Bottom</li>\n                        <li><code>padding: 10px 20px 15px 25px;</code> — Top | Right | Bottom | Left</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Remember:</strong> Padding increases the total size of the element (by default). A 300px wide box with 20px padding is actually 340px wide!\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>3. Border</h2>\n                <p>The border sits between padding and margin. It can be visible (styled) or invisible but still takes space.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Border shorthand: width style color */\n.box {\n  border: 2px solid #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Individual properties */\n.custom-border {\n  border-width: 2px;\n  border-style: solid;\n  border-color: #7C3AED;\n}\n\n/* Border styles */\n.style-examples {\n  border-style: solid;      /* Solid line */\n  border-style: dashed;     /* Dashed line */\n  border-style: dotted;     /* Dotted line */\n  border-style: double;     /* Double line */\n  border-style: groove;     /* 3D grooved */\n  border-style: ridge;      /* 3D ridged */\n  border-style: inset;      /* 3D inset */\n  border-style: outset;     /* 3D outset */\n  border-style: none;       /* No border */\n  border-style: hidden;     /* Hidden border */\n}\n\n/* Individual sides */\n.asymmetric {\n  border-top: 3px solid #7C3AED;\n  border-right: 1px dashed #ccc;\n  border-bottom: 2px dotted #999;\n  border-left: none;\n}\n\n/* Border radius (rounded corners) */\n.rounded {\n  border-radius: 8px;              /* All corners */\n}\n\n.circle {\n  border-radius: 50%;              /* Perfect circle (if square) */\n}\n\n.pill {\n  border-radius: 100px;            /* Pill shape */\n}\n\n/* Individual corners */\n.custom-radius {\n  border-radius: 10px 20px 10px 20px;\n  /*            top-left top-right bottom-right bottom-left */\n}\n\n/* Elliptical corners */\n.ellipse {\n  border-radius: 20px / 10px;      /* Horizontal / Vertical radius */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Border properties:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>border-width</code> — Thickness (px, em, thin, medium, thick)</li>\n                        <li><code>border-style</code> — solid, dashed, dotted, double, none</li>\n                        <li><code>border-color</code> — Any valid color</li>\n                        <li><code>border-radius</code> — Rounds the corners</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>4. Margin</h2>\n                <p>Margin creates space outside the border, separating elements from each other. Margins are transparent.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Margin - space outside the border */\n.box {\n  /* All sides equal */\n  margin: 20px;\n}\n\n/* Same shorthand patterns as padding */\n.card {\n  margin: 10px 20px 15px 25px;   /* Top Right Bottom Left */\n  margin: 10px 20px;              /* Vertical Horizontal */\n  margin: 10px 20px 15px;         /* Top Sides Bottom */\n}\n\n/* Individual sides */\n.custom-margin {\n  margin-top: 10px;\n  margin-right: 20px;\n  margin-bottom: 15px;\n  margin-left: 25px;\n}\n\n/* Auto margins for centering */\n.centered {\n  width: 300px;\n  margin-left: auto;\n  margin-right: auto;\n  /* OR shorthand */\n  margin: 0 auto;\n}\n\n/* Horizontal centering */\n.container {\n  max-width: 1200px;\n  margin: 0 auto;        /* Center horizontally */\n}\n\n/* Inline/Block margins */\n.horizontal-space {\n  margin-inline: auto;   /* Left/right in LTR */\n  margin-block: 20px;    /* Top/bottom */\n}\n\n/* Negative margins (overlap) */\n.overlap {\n  margin-top: -20px;     /* Pulls element up */\n}\n\n.pull-left {\n  margin-left: -10px;    /* Extends beyond container */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Margin behaviors:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>margin: auto</code> — Takes available space, used for centering</li>\n                        <li>Negative margins — Pull elements closer or extend beyond</li>\n                        <li>Percentages — Relative to parent\'s width</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>5. Margin Collapsing</h2>\n                <p>Vertical margins between block elements collapse into a single margin equal to the larger one.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Margin Collapsing Example */\n\n/* HTML */\n&lt;div class="box-one"&gt;Box 1&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;div class="box-two"&gt;Box 2&lt;/div&gt;\n\n/* CSS */\n.box-one {\n  margin-bottom: 30px;\n}\n\n.box-two {\n  margin-top: 20px;\n}\n\n/* Total space between them: 30px, NOT 50px! */\n/* The margins collapse to the larger value */\n\n/* Preventing margin collapse */\n.no-collapse-parent {\n  overflow: hidden;       /* Creates BFC */\n  /* OR */\n  display: flow-root;     /* Modern way to create BFC */\n}\n\n.no-collapse-child {\n  display: inline-block;  /* Inline-blocks don\'t collapse */\n}\n\n/* Margins DON\'T collapse when: */\n/* - Using Flexbox or Grid */\n/* - Parent has overflow: hidden/auto/scroll */\n/* - Parent has border or padding */\n/* - Elements are positioned or floated */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Margin collapse only happens:</strong> Between vertical margins of block elements in normal flow. Horizontal margins never collapse.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>6. Box Sizing</h2>\n                <p>The box-sizing property controls how total width/height is calculated.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* content-box (default) */\n.content-box {\n  box-sizing: content-box;    /* Default */\n  width: 300px;\n  padding: 20px;\n  border: 5px solid black;\n  /* Total width: 300 + 40 + 10 = 350px */\n}\n\n/* border-box (recommended) */\n.border-box {\n  box-sizing: border-box;     /* Width includes padding & border */\n  width: 300px;\n  padding: 20px;\n  border: 5px solid black;\n  /* Total width: 300px (padding and border are INSIDE) */\n  /* Content area: 300 - 40 - 10 = 250px */\n}\n\n/* Best practice: Apply border-box to all elements */\n*, *::before, *::after {\n  box-sizing: border-box;\n}\n\n/* Or inherit from html */\nhtml {\n  box-sizing: border-box;\n}\n*, *::before, *::after {\n  box-sizing: inherit;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="explanation">\n                    <strong>Why border-box is better:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Width you set is the total width</li>\n                        <li>Easier to calculate layouts</li>\n                        <li>Adding padding/border doesn\'t break layout</li>\n                        <li>Most CSS frameworks expect this</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>7. Display and Box Type</h2>\n                <p>The display property affects how the box model works for an element.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Block elements */\ndiv, p, h1, section {\n  /* display: block (default) */\n  /* - Take full width available */\n  /* - Start on new line */\n  /* - Width, height, margins all work */\n  /* - Can contain other block and inline elements */\n}\n\n/* Inline elements */\nspan, a, strong {\n  /* display: inline (default) */\n  /* - Only take needed width */\n  /* - Don\'t start new line */\n  /* - Width and height ignored */\n  /* - Vertical margins/padding work differently */\n}\n\n/* Inline-block */\n.button {\n  display: inline-block;\n  /* - Flows like inline */\n  /* - But respects width, height, margins like block */\n}\n\n/* None */\n.hidden {\n  display: none;\n  /* - Removes element from layout */\n  /* - No space reserved */\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>8. Outline vs Border</h2>\n                <p>Outline is similar to border but doesn\'t affect layout.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Outline - doesn\'t add to box size */\n:focus {\n  outline: 2px solid #7C3AED;\n  outline-offset: 2px;       /* Space between element and outline */\n}\n\n/* Differences between border and outline: */\n/* \n   BORDER:\n   - Part of the box model\n   - Takes up space\n   - Can have different sides\n   - Affects layout\n   \n   OUTLINE:\n   - NOT part of box model\n   - Doesn\'t take space\n   - Always same on all sides\n   - Doesn\'t affect layout\n   - Often used for focus states\n*/\n\n/* Remove default outline (add your own focus style!) */\n:focus {\n  outline: none;             /* Never do this without adding focus styles! */\n  box-shadow: 0 0 0 3px rgba(124, 58, 237, 0.5);\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section>\n                <h2>9. Box Model Debugging</h2>\n                <p>Browser DevTools make it easy to visualize the box model.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* How to debug box model issues: */\n\n/* 1. Right-click element → Inspect */\n/* 2. Look at the "Computed" panel */\n/* 3. See visual diagram of box model */\n/* 4. Hover over elements to see box highlighted */\n\n/* Common issues: */\n\n/* Element wider than expected */\n.too-wide {\n  box-sizing: border-box;    /* Fix: use border-box */\n  width: 100%;\n  padding: 20px;\n}\n\n/* Unexpected spacing */\n.weird-space {\n  /* Check for margin collapse */\n  /* Add overflow: hidden to parent */\n}\n\n/* Element not centering */\n.not-centering {\n  /* Must have a width */\n  width: 300px;\n  margin: 0 auto;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="practice">\n                <h2>🎯 Practice Exercise</h2>\n                <p>Create these boxes with specific sizes:</p>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>/* Challenge: Create boxes that look like this: */\n/*\n   A: Total width 300px, 20px padding, 2px border\n   B: 100px square content, 10px padding all sides, rounded corners\n   C: Centered box, 500px wide, 30px vertical margin\n*/\n\n/* Hint: Think about box-sizing! */\n\n/* Your CSS: */</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n            \n            <section class="summary">\n                <h2>📚 Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <ul>\n                    <li>Every element is a box with content, padding, border, and margin</li>\n                    <li>Padding is inside, margin is outside the border</li>\n                    <li>Use <code>box-sizing: border-box</code> for predictable sizing</li>\n                    <li>Margin collapse affects vertical margins between block elements</li>\n                    <li><code>margin: auto</code> centers block elements horizontally</li>\n                    <li>Outline doesn\'t affect layout, great for focus states</li>\n                    <li>Use DevTools to debug box model issues</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n        </div>\n        \n        <div class="lesson-navigation">\n            <a href="lesson3.html" class="btn-secondary">← Previous: Colors and Text</a>\n            <a href="lesson5.html" class="btn-primary">Next: Display Property →</a>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n    \n    <footer>\n        <p>&copy; 2024 Learner. Learn to code, one lesson at a time.</p>\n    </footer>\n</body>\n</html></create-file>\n</function_calls>'}
